I fell in love with Dutch Bros Coffee while on a trip to Scottsdale AZ, so when I heard they were opening a location in Apple Valley I was very excited.

The first month or so was great, lines were long but with the help of training crews from AZ the employees were able to keep it moving and delivering their hot delicious coffee. During that time I visited Dutch Bros eight or so times, leaving satisfied every time.

Unfortunately things have changed, the friendly, and professional training crews from AZ have left and the High Deserts finest are now in their place. Lines are backing up, less staff, more confusion, and worst of all room temperature coffee my last three visits!

I know Dutch Bros has the potential to to turn it around and when that day comes I‚Äôll be back, but for now I‚Äôll be going to Six Beans.</Text>

< text>
I love Dutch Bros. Coffee drive thru. which I first experienced in the Boise area.  It has never been bitter like its popular competitor. The  employers are mostly college kids that have been well trained in customer service.  I am so glad to see it now available in Ca. Would like to see them expand and come to the Big Bear area, currently providing only its popular Walmart- like proprietary competitor but with exclusively high end brick and mortar pricing. <Time>1613888562110< /Time><Resp>None</Resp><user>118406615368414521572< /user><Text>I was doing some home hunting in the area and looked for a good bite to eat and came across the gorgeous photos for Bites & Bashes. Oddly, what caught my eye out of all the items was the Korean Breakfast plate - a mixture of white rice, bulgogi, and eggs. It seemed so simple yet the pictures looked so gorgeous and I had to try and see if the taste matched the picture quality, and it did!

My Korean Breakfast plate variation was with egg whites (+$1 extra), white rice, and bulgogi. I loved the presentation full of small colorful flakes, making the egg whites (which I know are usually boring - I cook them every morning, so I would know!) into a really nice treat. What should otherwise be a simplistic plate turned out to be really nice and flavorful. The egg whites were fluffy. The white rice was cooked just right (not too soft or hard), and the bulgogi was super flavorful and juicy mixed with onions and giving flavor to the rest of the rice and egg whites. My only small observation was that it was a bit pricy compared to other locations with similar bowls although the flavor profile and attention to detail make sense. I'd love to see some hot sauce or gochujang included though to give it a bit more of a bold flavor profile.

Parking is a little tight. There is some parking in the back of the restaurant as well as street / neighborhood parking (note the neighborhood is a bit narrow street-wise).

The cashier was super nice, and it looked like they were doing a major photo shoot inside. There is also some outdoor seating.

Hope to come back in the near future to try some other dishes!<//Text><rating>5< /rating>< gmap_id>

This unbelievably hip and cute cafe is located in Lomita and I hope it‚Äôs here to stay! I loved all the food and drink explanations + the excitement behind all the dishes. The mother was the chef and she came out to make sure we were okay and enjoying the food. She was very proud to say that she raised her children on the food she had just made us. Delicious food from mama, I loved it. Everything had a comforting, yet complex flavor to each dish without anything overpowering each other.

In addition, I loved the vegan aspect of the drinks because they don‚Äôt use egg whites, they use aquafaba which is apparently a pea. It was fun learning about this new frothy trick from the owner! It‚Äôs definitely safe to bring your vegan pals here.

The crack fries were aptly named as they were definitely made with crack. ;)

They also add colorful flowers to drinks and dishes which I am always a huge fan of. I love color blasts in my food and there‚Äôs many to delight your eyes here! Thanks for the wonderful experience!

P A R K I N G:

It‚Äôs pretty crowded in the residential area so you may have to foot it. I suggest carpooling.<//Text>

< Text>
It's a nice, open room with plenty of tables and may even work for larger groups.
I knew before we arrived I'd be trying the Mama's Bolognese spaghetti and the Crack fries, she got the Asian Chicken Salad as there are few healthy choices for someone watching carbs.
So the first thing I tasted was the Crack fries and they didn't disappoint. She tried one which was her first mistake. They held true to their name and she struggled to keep her hands off.
Then there was the Bolognese spaghetti, real comfort food made with love. I already knew this was going to be one of my favorite places when suddenly she threw us a curve. She came out of the kitchen with a sample plate she wanted me to try. It was a churro pancake with whip cream and Jack Daniels syrup. Oh My God!!!
Anyway she didn't do well on her low carb diet today and I found a new favorite place to have lunch. She said the salad was refreshing and light. She would do it again.
The staff is super friendly and you won't go a minute without seeing them by your table.
We spent $14.50 for the salad, $16.00 for the spaghetti, $5.00 for the fries and $3.00 each for the tropical ice tea (also really good).
So $45.44 before tip so a little high for lunch but well worth it. I'm just gonna start telling people to try this because I'm impressed.< /Text>

<Review>I've been going to Westminster Veterinary Group since 2013 when I adopted a kitten from their sister organization WAGS. I have since moved from the area, but I still make the 20-30 min drive out to them for all of my cats' needs because they are awesome.

Everyone there is incredibly friendly and thoughtful. All of the doctors are kind and take the time to explain everything in easy to understand terms. Currently I make a point to try to see Dr. Rettig as she is so knowledgeable and friendly, but she isn't shy about giving an honest opinion which I really appreciate. It's also easy to make appointments and I get appointment reminders when my cats are due for check-ups and vaccinations. They also have an online store that makes it easy to get prescriptions for medications such as flea meds (and the vet will let me know if I pick one that doesn't seem right for my cat) and then set up recurring deliveries so I don't have to remember to buy them.

I recently went to an appointment for the first time during the pandemic and Westminster Vet had a whole system in place to minimize human contact. I went inside (wearing a mask) to drop off my kitty and then went outside to wait in my car. The vet called me on my cell phone to chat about her recommendations for my kitty, and then the front office staff called to confirm the cost and get approval to move forward. Then I got a text when I could come back inside (wearing a mask) to pay and pick up my kitty. Easy peasy!

It's often challenging to find a good vet, so I'm incredibly happy to have found such a great place with consistently excellent service.<//Review>< rate>

< text>
Womble is 100% her manic bitey little self again
After being brought in being according to the ER vets who had her overnight with a guarded poor prognosis from Parvo (PLEASE VACCINATE ON TIME, my laziness"it's just a couple weeks" cost me a suffering puppy and the financial equivalent of a decent used car) I watched daily as my baby went from lethargically lifting head to greet me, to walking to me, to running to me, and the night before coming home running to me and jumping up and doing her shake shake dance.
Besides the fact that they saved my baby, I am so glad I picked Westminster because of some big differencces between them & other local vets I have been to.
#1) I am lucky, I have decent credit and had never needed it.. I got a loan to get THE BEST most intensive care, however...had I not been able to, they had other good options available, that would have also likely been successful, at much lower cost. Most vets "oh she has parvo..this is our protocol" with no discussion or personal plan. I never felt like money was the primary factor in anything Westminster Vetrinary did, I can NOT say that about some other local vets.
#2) Visiting your pet (if you are not intrusive etc) is ENCOURAGED (other 2 clinics..it's never allowed...I find that suspect, and also I feel like your pets morale is boosted by visiting, and any injury or illness is better recovered from when you are emotionally happy) we visited Womble at least twice daily for an hour or so, and I think it made her stay happier, even at her sickest to know that it was never going to be long before mama or papa would be there to hold her.
3) Overall environment.
It's clean. It doesn't smell like a barn or have metal chairs. I also loved wombles isolation icu room. A real little room with blanket nests and a bed and toys (yes you can bring from home, and they will also get blanket and toy from vet) food water , room to get up and walk (or run ..Womble is 7lbs so it was a master suite for her) I REALLY liked that she didn't have to see or hear other animals..
4) Staff. I can't say that there was anyone on staff I didn't like(I usually can find someone to dislike lol) everyone seems like they are really at the job they want to be at. I had the most interaction with Sebastian the Vet assistant who was Wombles main human for most of the stuff, he was incredibly knowledgeable about everything (full veterinarians were always accessible, and would call with update/come see me at visits) and he spent a lot of time with Womble and made her toys and he really loves animals/his job/has great people skills too. Both vetrinarians were wonderful. I brought Womble in with an hour notice, from a vet that gave her below 30% survival. Dr Tran came in, and said"I cannot guarantee that she will survive yet, but I practiced in Texas, where we have a lot of parvo puppies (I have spent time in Texas, this is true) I have an 80-90% success rate, Womble is otherwise healthy, she should be able to get through this fine" She also went over the other much cheaper options that still had a very good chance. She was friendly and happy and approachable and got on the floor with Womble and just the same feeling that I got from everyone there... working in Vetrinary medicine is what she does because it's what she wants to do, money is not a driving factor.
I will stop my essay now...but really I cannot say enough good things about you guys. Womble is sleeping happily after attacking her cat brothers and sisters and running and jumping and doing her shake shake dance and eating all day.10 days ago she was so sick we thought she might die on the way to the vet. The treatment for parvo is not fun for the puppy, but they made it as happy and comfortable as possible. For the humans too
And Dr Hueston sorry I didn't mention you, but you were great too, and always on top of it with updates.< /text>

< Review>
Dr Greenberg is one of the most respected vets in the country and for good reason.

I am shocked at the bad reviews. It leads me to believe that the money may have been more of an issue to you than your pets welfare. I have never experienced a test that I felt was unnecessary. I hate forking out money but I do it without consideration for the welfare of my kids. Just ask my Care Credit Card.
This is one of the few vets around that cares about the animals and not the money. But realize this is a business and without money they cannot function.

The front desk, most Techs and the Vets know myself and my wife by first name and every single pet we have, Koda, Renji, Skittle-butt, Nani, Scruffy, Toffee and Charmin. How many Vets do you see who need to look at a chart just to remember your name? and still pronounce it wrong. I have even had calls from Dr Greenberg just to see how my kids are doing.

I have nothing but respect for Westminster Veterinary Group and you will be doing your pet a great favor by trusting them.</Review>
